    <li> I had only moderate hopes when I bought this, and WOW am I impressed! The curls it creates are amazing, and they hold like curls never have before! I have fine, straight, long hair. Normally, my curls will fall flat within a few hours, even WITH hairspray or other products. These curls held ALL day, with NO products, on the first try! I&#x27;m honestly a bit baffled, because I never thought that was a possibility for my hair. I don&#x27;t know what it is about this iron/wand that does the trick, but I&#x27;m ecstatic!     I bought this iron because my husband bought the Remington Pearl rollers for me a while back. That was one of the first appliances to really curl my hair, and I&#x27;ve tried everything. Based on that and the price of the wand (cheaper than the rollers) I had to give this a try, despite all the burn warnings I&#x27;ve seen in reviews. I&#x27;m not a professional by any means, (and I&#x27;m rather clumsy) but I&#x27;ve used this wand several times without incident. I AM, however, accustomed to wrapping my hair around the barrel of regular irons, so I didn&#x27;t have any difficulty getting used to that. I have yet to burn myself, because the wand never touches my skin. I can see how if it did, however, it would result in some nasty burns, especially on higher heat settings. Be careful, ladies! I also have yet to wear the glove that comes with this. I tried the lowest heat setting the first time I used it, and it worked perfectly, so I don&#x27;t feel the need to turn it up. I think too often people decide to crank the heat settings as high as they will go, without testing first. This wand will reach 410 degrees, and I don&#x27;t think that&#x27;s necessary for most hair types. Start at the lowest settings, and work your way up. If you&#x27;ve never wrapped your hair this way, DEFINITELY wear the glove, especially if you use higher settings. So far, I don&#x27;t need the glove, and doubt that I ever will. If you&#x27;re having problems maneuvering the wand or burning yourself, try practicing with it off. Might help.    The wand is super lightweight, easy to maneuver, and works better than any curling iron I&#x27;ve ever owned. It heats quickly, works quickly, the buttons are well placed/made (I don&#x27;t accidentally turn the iron off) and you can \\&quot;lock-in\\&quot; the heat setting so you can&#x27;t accidentally change them while curling. Also, my hair doesn&#x27;t have that strange burned smell it always has with other irons, including ceramic ones. I just can&#x27;t say enough good things about this wand. Even after a blow out I was able to curl all of my hair fairly easily in a short amount of time. The results you can get with this iron are countless, from small, springy curls(wrap only around the smallest part of the wand and hold tight) to beachy loose waves(hold the wand downwards and wrap starting from the thickest section to the smallest and hold loosly for like a second). One tip, for those of you with layers in your hair, it may be easier NOT to section off your hair, and if not easier the results will def. be more natural looking. When I sectioned my hair to begin with, it was quite difficult to get a good section of hair to curl and when I was done it looked \\&quot;fake\\&quot;. The glove that comes with it is much easier to use than other gloves you can buy at the store because they tend to be thicker, with an odd texture that your hair will stick to and become frizzy. This one is sleek enough to not add frizz and protects your hand from the heat of the iron(which is very hot!). I noticed people complaining about the glove not protecting their hand from the heat and I think this has to do with how long you are holding your hair on the wand. That is a user mistake and should not be blamed on Remington or their heat protector glove-thingamajig. If you have the iron on the right temp. setting for your hair(can take some time to get it right) you only need to hold each strand around the wand for a few seconds to get a perfect curl, and in my experience if you hold the curl for too long it looks strangely unnatural. Another thing I want to add is be careful because there are dozens of opportunities to burn yourself while using this. I know that goes for any styling tool that heats up but I read over 10 reviews of people complaining of the burn risk, use some common sense people and be diligent and dont rag on Remington for your own mistake(i own an expensive straightener, which was an upgrade from a remington one and I experienced the same amount of burns from both). I love this product but I did recieve a nasty burn on my leg(from not paying attention) and a small burn on my forehead while curling my bangs (just because I wasnt used to it yet). It is just a risk you take when using ANY heated tool.</li>

    <li> A lot of unsatisfied people talk about the hair not staying on the barrel or hair not being wound tight enough, etc. Are people just winding it around the barrel and then letting go of their hair right away? Every section I grab, I twist my hair in the opposite direction around the barrel (this prevents your curls from falling into each other if that makes sense).     <li> (Not using the Remington Iron) --&gt;  My hair is not thin, but not thick.. However it has never held curls. I&#x27;d used a curling iron for years and the only thing I used to get to stay were curled under short bangs with a lot of hairspray.  (Told ya I been using irons for years lol) A few weeks ago, I wanted to try curling my hair (its been such a job to do, that I don&#x27;t do it very often) to go out that night. I spent 2 hours trying to get my hair to curl, using product on each strand and then curling it and then spraying again, my hands were a big sticky mess with product from a high end salon that states its Not Sticky. (I&#x27;ve tried sprays, mousses, etc) Holding each strand I curled on the iron for 60 seconds at least! By the time I got all the way around my head, the other sides curls have come completely undone. I&#x27;ve been searching for something since, to try to get the long luscious curls that I&#x27;ve been wanting.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;(Using the Remington Iron) --&gt; I got on youtube and started looking at how girls get the curls I been wanting. People seemed successful with this style of iron. So I went ahead and bought one from Target cause I didn&#x27;t want to wait to have it shipped, although, amazon and target  had the same price. It was evening time and I thought I&#x27;d just try to curl it to see how it did before I went to bed, and I started curling my hair (my hair is about 3 inches past my shoulders), without ANY product other than some Tressemee Heat Protectant spray, I started to wind my hair around the iron. I held it for 7 seconds, and let go. I had a bouncy tight curl!  This iron states that if you use a larger section you will have a looser curl, and smaller section will produce a tighter curl.  I&#x27;d never used a iron before without a clip. And let me just say that I find it WAY easier to hold the iron and wind my hair around it, rather than putting an iron around my hair, making sure the clamp holds my hair right so the end isn&#x27;t all jacked up, and then winding it up, etc. This thing, you just hold the iron, spin your hair around, hold a FEW seconds, let go, all is done!!! It&#x27;s so much quicker, it&#x27;s hotter than most other irons, no fussing with clamps, and it actually works. I continued going around in sections around the lower half of my hair, and the curls I made were still holding up, I really couldn&#x27;t believe it. I finished my entire head of hair, in about 30 minutes (my first time!) and all the curls held up, Even those small sections I did with tight curls, still tight. You can loosen them some if you run your hands thru it but they&#x27;re still holding the curl. When I finished I had this moment, remembering the girl spending hours doing my hair for my wedding day trying to get it to hold curl, and telling me, \\&quot;I&#x27;m sorry but it&#x27;s just not staying.\\&quot; (I ended up with VERY loose hardly noticeable waves at my wedding) I wasn&#x27;t surprised then, but now I&#x27;m thinking, where was this iron then!! Lol. So please know, that on the hardest to curl hair, this iron really does its job. The next morning, I got up to look in the mirror, and my hair was still very very curly. Just amazing. I know I will never go back to any other iron they make.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Also those of you concerned with burning (as I was) this iron comes with a heat protectant glove. It&#x27;s not like a thick oven glove or anything, its like a satin type finish (so its not going to pull your hair with it on, you can run your fingers thru your hair with it). I thought it was nice the iron came with a protectant, especially for those who are so worried about TRYING this style of iron (as I was). But once I got going, I got quicker and I forgot I even had a glove to try. So I didn&#x27;t end up using it, so I can&#x27;t tell you how well it serves it purpose, but it does have a note with it in the box stating that you can&#x27;t hold the iron with it for a long time, as you will probably get burned. But if you just had it on there so if you bumped the iron it should save you from that burn.. This thing, you just hold the iron, spin your hair around, hold a FEW seconds, let go, all is done!!! It&#x27;s so much quicker, it&#x27;s hotter than most other irons, no fussing with clamps, and it actually works. I continued going around in sections around the lower half of my hair, and the curls I made were still holding up, I really couldn&#x27;t believe it. I finished my entire head of hair, in about 30 minutes (my first time!) and all the curls held up, Even those small sections I did with tight curls, still tight. You can loosen them some if you run your hands thru it but they&#x27;re still holding the curl.     <li> I have to say, curling irons were not like this in my day.  There I was.  13.  Woefully fine, limp hair.  It was the 80&#x27;s, you know, and this was NOT the time for such lifeless locks.  Do you think I didn&#x27;t try?  Of course I did.  I diligently used my little spring clamp 1986 conair trying to force my hair into beautiful springy 1986 curls every morning, only to walk outside into the terrarium of 40% humidity known as Houston,TX, and have it all fall flat.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Eventually I discovered the perm and I thought I&#x27;d died and gone to heaven.  At some point, though, I had to break the cycle of perms and let my hair grow out.  I&#x27;ve come to terms w/ buns and ponytails as my everyday style.  I am 41 and married so who cares.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My viable supermodelling years are behind me now, but even so, I like to keep abreast of the latest in beauty and hair.  I came across these wands on such a forum and they piqued my interest.  I tried to ignore them, recalling the ineffective iron of yesteryear and all of the time it frittered away.  Eventually though, my weakness and vanity overcame me and I ordered this pretty pink wand, hopeful, excited and confused about the lack of clamp.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;She came to me on an otherwise bleak Tuesday, in the typical speedy manner (thank you Amazon).  I snatched her up and stole away to the lavatory for some private time.  And.... it was pretty good.  The curls I managed LASTED, and that was a miracle!  I slept on it and touched them up the next morning - fabulous!  But my technique needed some work.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This wand has simple intuitive controls.  You&#x27;ll press the power button and press the plus or minus button to adjust to the temperature you want.  It will display graduated bars that blink until it reaches the selected temp.  You hold the wand horizontally or vertically (you&#x27;ll find different positions work better on different parts of the head) and wind about an 1\\&quot; section of hair around it, starting at the wider base, holding the end as close as comfortable to the tip of the iron.  Leave for about 5 seconds, more or less as needed (but not TOO long, to avoid scorching) and then release.  Some people pin the curl in place to cool, some let the curl fall into their palm to let cool w/o stretching and some just let it go.  I separate my fine hair into 4 to 6 sections and pin them out of the way, and release and work one section at a time.  Ambidexterity is a plus, but not required.  To turn the wand off, hold the power button down for several seconds.  This design prevents accidental shutoff which is a problem w/ some irons.  The only real difficulty I have is w/ the conical shape, as the hair tends to all slide up toward the tip and decreases the curling space.  I have since ordered the \\&quot;elliptical\\&quot; version of the Pearl series and don&#x27;t have this issue w/ it.  I now use both in one session, as I like the pointy end of the conical for doing the underneath hair close to my neck and the stuff and my temples, and use the elliptical for the back and most of the crown.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Please note, these new fancy wands get HOT.  This one goes up in increments to 410 I believe, which is one hot mother.  Also, the aforementioned lack of clamp means plenty of up close and personal time w/ the hot iron.  It does come w/ the heat glove and of course you are encouraged to use that.  I find it a bit cumbersome and find myself curling w/o it most of the time.  As my technique improves I find myself burning fingers and neck much less.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you haven&#x27;t used this type of iron before, I recommend watching several of the slew of the videos out there on the subject.  I also purchased a neck protector, which I imagine one could easily make at home if one weren&#x27;t so darn lazy. The one I purchased is made of heat resistant materials, though, which is a bonus.  I hope w/ practice to reduce the iron-to-skin contact incidents, but the last burn on my neck was of such severity that I purchased the protector.  HOT.&lt;br/&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Now, the heat obviously can damage hair w/ repeated use, and if you&#x27;re like me, you are going to want to use this thing ALL THE TIME.  This will require a good heat protectant, something w/ silicones and oils rather than water, regular use of a good moisturizing treatment and frequent trims.  Use it on the lowest effective setting possible and never use on damp hair.  I understand that ceramic irons are less damaging than the others (chrome?) but heat is damaging regardless, so take the necessary precautions and care and try to not use it in conjunction w/ other damaging treatments and not daily.  I am trying to dial back my usage but it works so beautifully it&#x27;s difficult!</li>

I did not think to use the glove.  You don&#x27;t need to hold the hair with your fingers against the iron.  You just maintain the appropriate angle and leverage, and hold onto the very tip of the hair lock.  Watch some videos and you&#x27;ll have an ah-HA moment.  At one point I did hold my hair to the wand with my bare fingers, just to see what people were experiencing and I still have fingertips and everything.  This tool&#x27;s temperatures fall within a normal range, for contemporary standards - it&#x27;s like using a CHI flat iron.  If it&#x27;s not hot enough for you, or is heating slowly, I think you just got a defective one.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As far as burning yourself goes, I think different people have different spacial awarenesses.  I don&#x27;t seem to know where my forehead is, so I burn it all the time with my straightener.  But my hands and arms were never remotely at risk with this iron, and since the tip was pointing away from my head, I was unlikely to brush against my ears or face.  What I&#x27;m trying to say is: what is dangerous for one person might be easy for you, so don&#x27;t give any review too much weight.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Obviously don&#x27;t leave the thing plugged in around children or resting with its heating element against a burnable surface.  Is this the criteria we are using to review styling tools now?  Let&#x27;s all just agree that heating elements should be used responsibly (read: with a degree of paranoia) and that no product design is going to save you if you do something careless/irresponsible.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Argument 2: Does not work with layers!  -and- Need to be an expert to use!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I was inspired to buy this because I was watching a YouTube tutorial employing this type of curling iron. Yes, I am dumb enough to be foiled by a proper curling iron, but do not let people tell you that you need to be advanced to use this one!  Look at the numbers.  Maybe you will be one of the 4% who find it awkward.  But the odds are in your favor!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As far as layers go, mine are pretty overkill atm and I just didn&#x27;t feel hindered by them at all.  I would say... can you figure out how to maneuver your layers when styling your hair normally - like if you were to do a braided updo or something?  If you can, they won&#x27;t suddenly become a problem for you in this situation.     <li> First of all, after buying and using this wand, I feel obligated to put a few of the exaggerated negative reviews about the actual use of this tool to rest. This is just like using any other curling iron, but you wrap your hair around the wand starting from the top of the head rather than at the bottom with a clamp holding the section of hair in place. If you are concerned about burning yourself on this wand, use a lower heat setting. There are plenty of heat settings available. That being said, this is not a curling iron for beginners. Maybe you should consider using curlers instead or starting out with a clamp style wand.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I bought this curling iron because the reviews all claimed the \\&quot;natural\\&quot; look of these big to small curls.
